            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Association for the Advancement of Science</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review with 24 refs. of mechanisms for lithium insertion in carbonaceous materials.  Lithium can be inserted reversibly within most carbonaceous materials.  The phys. mechanism for this insertion depends on the carbon type.  Lithium intercalates in layered carbons, e.g., graphite, and it adsorbs on the surfaces of single carbon layers in nongraphitizable hard carbons.  Lithium also appears to reversibly bind near hydrogen atoms in carbonaceous materials contg. substantial hydrogen, which are made by heating org. precursors to temps. near 700°.  Each of these three classes of materials is suitable for use as anode in advanced lithium batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref4" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1038/s41467-018-06126-z"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guan, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ming, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mai, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Lithiophilic-lithiophobic Gradient Interfacial Layer for a Highly Stable Lithium Metal Anode</span>. <i>Nat.                         cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Lithiophilic-lithiophobic gradient interfacial layer for a highly stable lithium metal anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang Huimin; Xiang Yu; Li Meng; Zhang Wenfeng; Zhu Xiayu; Ming Hai; Lu Lin; Qiu Jingyi; Cao Gaoping; Yang Yusheng; Zhang Hao; Zhang Huimin; Liao Xiaobin; Mai Liqiang; Liao Xiaobin; Zhao Yan; Guan Yuepeng; Huang Yaqin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3729</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">The long-standing issue of lithium dendrite growth during repeated deposition or dissolution processes hinders the practical use of lithium-metal anodes for high-energy density batteries.  Here, we demonstrate a promising lithiophilic-lithiophobic gradient interfacial layer strategy in which the bottom lithiophilic zinc oxide/carbon nanotube sublayer tightly anchors the whole layer onto the lithium foil, facilitating the formation of a stable solid electrolyte interphase, and prevents the formation of an intermediate mossy lithium corrosion layer.  Together with the top lithiophobic carbon nanotube sublayer, this gradient interfacial layer can effectively suppress dendrite growth and ensure ultralong-term stable lithium stripping/plating.  This strategy is further demonstrated to provide substantially improved cycle performance in copper current collector, 10 cm(2) pouch cell and lithium-sulfur batteries, which, coupled with a simple fabrication process and wide applicability in various materials for lithium-metal protection, makes the lithiophilic-lithiophobic gradient interfacial layer a favored strategy for next-generation lithium-metal batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref5" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201703268"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Saurel, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Orayech, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Carriazo, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rojo, T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">From Charge Storage Mechanism to Performance: A Roadmap toward High Specific Energy Sodium-Ion Batteries through Carbon Anode Optimization</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Understanding High-Energy-Density Sn4P3 Anodes for Potassium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Wenchao; Pang, Wei Kong; Sencadas, Vitor; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Joule</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1534-1547</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Phosphorus-based anodes for alkali metal-ion batteries are attractive due to their high theor.-specific capacity.  However, their poor electrochem. performance caused by relatively large vol. variations during cycling, low elec. cond., and severe electrolyte decompn. due to highly reactive phosphide surface hinder their potential applications.  Herein, we confine Sn4P3 in N-doped carbon fibers as anode for potassium-ion batteries with enhanced cycling stability and high rate capability (160.7 mA hr g-1 after 1,000 cycles at 500 mA g-1).  The Sn4P3 anodes undergo a sequential conversion (P to K3P11, K3P) and alloying (Sn to KSn) reactions with synergistic K-storage mechanisms.  Also, the electrolyte with potassium bis(fluorosulfonyl)imide salt can effectively suppress the dendrite growth in K stripping/plating, stabilize the solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI) layer, and avoid excessive side reactions, thus enhancing the electrode stability.  This work provides a feasible approach to overcome the durability bottlenecks of K-ion batteries through regulating dendrite growth and SEI formation.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref9" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1021/jacs.6b12185"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Phosphorus-Based Alloy Materials for Advanced Potassium-Ion Battery Anode</span>. <i>J. The Sn4P3/C composite is investigated as a novel anode material for PIBs.  The electrode delivered a reversible capacity of 384.8 mA h g-1 at 50 mA g-1 and a good rate capability of 221.9 mA h g-1, even at 1 A g-1.  Its electrochem. performance is better than any anode material reported so far for PIBs.  It was also found that the Sn4P3/C electrode displays a discharge potential plateau of 0.1 V in PIBs, slightly higher than for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) (0.01 V), and well above the plating potential of metal.  This diminishes the formation of dendrites during cycling, and thus Sn4P3 is a relatively safe anode material, esp. for application in large-scale energy storage, where large amts. of electrode materials are used.  Furthermore, a possible reaction mechanism of the Sn4P3/C composite as PIB anode is proposed.  This work may open up a new avenue for further development of alloy-based anodes with high capacity and long cycle life for PIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref10" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms5033"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Matsuda, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ishii, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cumings, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Expanded Graphite as Superior Anode for Sodium-ion Batteries</span>. <i>Nat.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphite, as the most common anode for com. Li-ion batteries, has been reported to have a very low capacity when used as a Na-ion battery anode.  It is well known that electrochem. insertion of Na+ into graphite is significantly hindered by the insufficient interlayer spacing.  Here we report expanded graphite as a Na-ion battery anode.  Prepd. through a process of oxidn. and partial redn. on graphite, expanded graphite has an enlarged interlayer lattice distance of 4.3 Å yet retains an analogous long-range-ordered layered structure to graphite.  In situ transmission electron microscopy has demonstrated that the Na-ion can be reversibly inserted into and extd. from expanded graphite.  Galvanostatic studies show that expanded graphite can deliver a high reversible capacity of 284 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 20 mA g-1, maintain a capacity of 184 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1, and retain 73.92% of its capacity after 2,000 cycles.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref11" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201403734"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jache, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Adelhelm, P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Use of Graphite as a Highly Reversible Electrode with Superior Cycle Life for Sodium-Ion Batteries by Making Use of Co-Intercalation Phenomena</span>. <i>Angew.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The energy crisis and environmental pollution require the advancement of large-scale energy storage techniques.  Among the various commercialized technologies, batteries have attracted enormous attention due to their relatively high energy d. and long cycle life.  Nevertheless, the limited supply and uneven distribution of lithium minerals, as well as their high cost, has greatly hindered the application of lithium-ion batteries in large-scale energy storage.  Therefore, building next-generation alternative rechargeable batteries that feature low cost, long service life, and high safety is of the utmost importance.  Over the past several years, we have witnessed many successful research outcomes for sodium and potassium ion batteries (SIBs and PIBs) in regard to electrode and electrolyte materials.  In this Perspective, we summarize the current developments on SIBs/PIBs and their challenges when facing practical applications, including their cost, energy d., ion diffusivity in solids/electrolytes/interphases, cycle life, and safety concerns. Nitrogen sorption shows the carbon-enriched mesopores with a sp. surface area of 113 m2 g-1.  The XPS anal. indicates that the carbon has a high nitrogen content of 7.78 at.%, in the forms of pyridinic and pyrrolic, as well as graphitic nitrogen.  The nitrogen-rich mesoporous carbon shows a high reversible capacity of 338 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 30 mA g-1, and good rate performance as well as ultralong cycling durability (110.7 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 500 mA g-1 over 800 cycles).  The excellent sodium storage performance of the nitrogen-rich mesoporous carbon is attributed to its disordered structure with large interlayer distance, interconnected porosity, and the enriched nitrogen heteroatoms.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref16" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1039/C9TA09984K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ming, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ming, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, R.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Advances in Nanostructured Carbon for Sodium-ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review. In recent years, significant progress of Na ion battery anodes, which restricted the development of SIBs in the past decades, was achieved.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbons attract myriad interest as anode materials for high-energy rechargeable batteries due to their low costs and high theor. capacities; practically, they deliver unsatisfactory performance due to their intrinsically disordered microarchitecture.  Here a facile ion-catalyzed synthesis is reported of a phenol-formaldehyde resin-based hard-carbon aerogel that takes advantage of the chelation effect of phenol and Fe3+, which consists of a three-dimensionally interconnected carbon network embedded with hydrogen-rich, ordered microstructures of expanded nanographites and carbon micropores. The structural merits of the carbon offer chances to achieve lithium/sodium storage performance far beyond that possible with the conventional carbon anode materials, including graphite and mesocarbon microbeads, along with fast kinetics and long cycle life. Despite this, the absence of a suitable neg. electrode material hinders their development.  In this contribution, the authors synthesized monodispersed hard carbon spherules (HCS) from an abundant biomass of sucrose, and studied the influence of the carbonization temp. on the microstructure and electrochem. performance.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Coupled Carbonization Strategy toward Advanced Hard Carbon for High-Energy Sodium-Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Huimin; Ming, Hai; Zhang, Wenfeng; Cao, Gaoping; Yang, Yusheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are expected to be a promising com. alternative to lithium-ion batteries for grid electricity storage due to their potential low cost in the near future.  Up to the present, the anode material still remains a great challenge for the application of SIBs, esp. at room temp.  Graphite has an obvious limitation to store larger radius sodium ions (Na+) in comparison with lithium ions (Li+), while the hard carbon with large interlayer distance can demonstrate a relatively high storage capability and durable cycle life.  However, the disadvantages of low initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) mainly caused by large surface area and high cost synthetic approach hinder its practical applications.  Herein, a new coupled carbonization strategy is presented to prep. a cost-effective hard carbon material by pyrolyzing and carbonizing the mixt. of abundant sucrose and phenolic resin.  Benefiting from the specialized pyrolysis reaction process and optimized conditions as studied in detail, the hard carbon has an extremely low surface area of 1.54 m2 g-1 and high initial Coulombic efficiency of 87%, which have been rarely reported before and enhance the utilization efficiency of Na+ consumption within the cathode in the future.  More importantly, the hard carbon, with a high interlayer distance 3.95 Å, can deliver a higher capacity of 319 mAh/g and maintain a finer capacity retention of 90% over 150 cycles.  Besides, a full cell with the configuration of as-prepd. hard carbon anode vs. an air-stable O3-Na0.9[Cu0.22Fe0.30Mn0.48]O2 cathode is further presented, and it has a high ICE of 80% and energy d. of 256 Wh kganode-1 (vs hard carbon) with reliable cycle performance.  The results demonstrate that our synthetic strategy is feasible and extendable, while the tunable carbon-based materials should have wider applications in addn. to the attractive properties in Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref21" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemrev.5b00345"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Upton, B. As the most accessible, renewable form of carbon (in comparison to CO2), lignocellulosic biomass (defined as org. matter available on a renewable basis) has been acknowledged as the most logical carbon-based feedstock for a variety of materials such as biofuels and chems.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Nitrogen-contg. hollow carbon microspheres (NHCSs) are prepd. by a modified template method in the presence of resorcinol/formaldehyde as carbon precursors and ethylenediamine (EDA) as both a base catalyst and nitrogen precursor.  The NHCSs are used as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries, showing a superior reversible discharge capacity of 334 mAh g-1 after 100 cycles at 50 mA g-1.  A high reversible discharge capacity of 114 mAh g-1 can also be obtained even at an extremely high c.d. of 10 A g-1.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Scalable synthesis of hierarchical macropore-rich activated carbon microspheres assembled by carbon nanoparticles for high rate performance supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Dongdong; Zhao, Jianghong; Feng, Chong; Zhao, Rijie; Sun, Yahui; Guan, Taotao; Han, Baixin; Tang, Nan; Wang, Jianlong; Li, Kaixi; Qiao, Jinli; Zhang, Jiujun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">342</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A scalable inverse-microemulsion-polymn.-phase-sepn. coupling method is applied to successfully prep. hierarchical macropore-rich activated carbon microspheres (ACS) using a phenolic resin (PR) precursor followed by carbonization and KOH activation for the first time.  The formed ACS materials are assembled by carbon nanoparticles (CNPs).  The macropores interspersed among the component CNPs are formed after removing the non-reactive solvent phase in the course of the polymn. of the reactive PR phase, which occupies ∼64% of the total pore vol. (∼2.779 cm3 g-1) of the optimized ACS.  In combination with mesopores (∼18% of the total pore vol.), the ACS possesses meso/macropores approaching 82% of the total pore vol.  Micropores are created in the component CNPs via KOH activation, showing shortened ion transport distances in the nanoscale dimension.  Both the hierarchical micro/meso/macroporous structure and the inner nanoparticle morphol. (short ion diffusion pathways) can significantly contribute to the rapid transport of electrolyte ions throughout the carbonaceous matrix, resulting in superior rate performance of ACS-based supercapacitors.  More importantly, the energy densities of the ACS supercapacitors operating in both aq. and org. electrolyte retain steady over a wide range of power densities varying dramatically from 0.25 to 14.5 kW kg-1 and to 7.0 kW kg-1, resp.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref27" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2016.07.034"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Duan, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Unique Elastic N-doped Carbon Nanofibrous Microspheres with Hierarchical Porosity Derived from Renewable Chitin for High Rate Supercapacitors</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>27</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">482</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">491</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Unique elastic N-doped carbon nanofibrous microspheres with hierarchical porosity derived from renewable chitin for high rate supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Duan, Bo; Gao, Xiang; Yao, Xu; Fang, Yan; Huang, Liang; Zhou, Jun; Zhang, Lina</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Chitin derived from discarded seafood waste (crab and shrimp shell) is a naturally abundant resource, but its difficult dissoly. limits the processing and applications.  Herein, we prepd. nanofibrous microspheres by using chitin soln. dissolved in NaOH/urea aq. solvent at low temp., and subsequently fabricated the novel elastic nitrogen-doped carbon microspheres by pyrolyzing the chitin microspheres.  Interestingly, the carbon microspheres were consisted of robust cross-linked nanofibers and displayed interconnected nanofibrous framework architecture, named as CNFF.  The CNFF microspheres showed unique elasticity, excellent compression behaviors, and the morphol. recovered completely over 5 cyclic compression at strain 75%.  Moreover, the carbon microspheres exhibited an outstanding rate capability with a capacitance retention of ∼50% when increase the scan rate from 5 mV/s to 10,000 mV/s as well as good cycling stability for supercapacitor applications, as a result of their hierarchical porosity, stable 3D interconnected mesh structure and ultrahigh sp. surface area (over 1000 m2/g).  Particularly, in the org. electrolyte, the highest deliverable energy d. reached up to 58.7 Wh/kg.  This work opened up a completely new and green avenue for constructing high performance carbon-based material with elasticity from biomass waste, showing promising application in the energy storage field.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref28" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2015.10.045"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qi, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiao, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Novel N-doped Porous Carbon Microsphere Composed of Hollow Carbon Nanospheres</span>. <i>Carbon</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>96</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">864</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">870</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

By spraying the precursor soln. into a high-temp. chamber, micrometer-scale hollow structure can be immediately obtained.  To achieve the required morphol., the factors of influencing the products morphol. and purity are systematically optimized.  The as-obtained HPMs have a low bulk d. of 0.089 g/cm3, narrow particle size distribution of 15-80 μm with a mean size of 37 μm, a high floatation ratio of 96.3% and high mech. strength. As a proof-of-concept application, a series of syntactic foam consisting of HPMs and HCMs as fillers and phenolic resin as matrix are prepd. via a hot-press molding.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical performance of electrospun carbon nanofibers as free-standing and binder-free anodes for sodium-ion and lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jin, Juan; Shi, Zhi-qiang; Wang, Cheng-yang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A series of hard carbon nanofiber-based electrodes derived from electrospun polyacrylonitrile nanofibers have been fabricated by stabilization in air at about 280° and then carbonization in N2 at heat treatment temps. between 800 and 1500°.  The electrochem. performances of the binder-free, current collector-free carbon nanofiber-based anodes in lithium-ion batteries and sodium-ion batteries are systematically investigated and compared.  We demonstrate the presence of similar alkali metal insertion mechanisms in both cases, but just the differences of the layer spacing and pore size available for lithium and sodium ion lead the discharge capacity delivered at sloping region and plateau region to vary from the kinds of alkali elements.  Although the anodes in sodium-ion batteries show poorer rate capability than that in lithium-ion batteries, they still achieve a reversible sodium intercalation capacity of 275 mA-h/g and similar cycling stability due to the conductive three-dimensional network, weakly ordered turbostratic structure and a large interlayer spacing between graphene sheets.  The feature of high capacity and stable cycling performance makes polyacrylonitrile-based carbon nanofibers to be promising candidates as electrodes in rechargeable sodium-ion batteries and lithium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref38" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.10.034"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Henderson, W.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hard carbon nanoparticles as high-capacity, high-stability anodic materials for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiao, Lifen; Cao, Yuliang; Henderson, Wesley A.; Sushko, Maria L.; Shao, Yuyan; Xiao, Jie; Wang, Wei; Engelhard, Mark H.; Nie, Zimin; Liu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon nanoparticles (HCNP) were synthesized by the pyrolysis of a polyaniline precursor.  The measured Na+ cation diffusion coeff. (10-13-10-15 cm2 s-1) in the HCNP obtained at 1150 °C is two orders of magnitude lower than that of Li+ in graphite (10-10-10-13 cm2 s-1), indicating that reducing the carbon particle size is very important for improving electrochem. performance.  These measurements also enable a clear visualization of the stepwise reaction phases and rate changes which occur throughout the insertion/extn. processes in HCNP, The electrochem. measurements also show that the nano-sized HCNP obtained at 1150 °C exhibited higher practical capacity at voltages lower than 1.2 V (vs. Na/Na+), as well as a prolonged cycling stability, which is attributed to an optimum spacing of 0.366 nm between the graphitic layers and the nano particular size resulting in a low-barrier Na+ cation insertion.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Amorphous C-based anode materials are considered as one of the most promising candidates for Na-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, there are 2 main barriers before large-scale industrialization, i.e. low initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) and high cost caused by low C yield of precursors.  The authors report a novel com. activated amorphous C-based anode synthesized through a facile-tailored strategy consisting of annealing and surface coating.  The as-prepd. amorphous C has a porous internal structure but a low sp. surface area (SSA) with a dense surface C layer.  As an anode material for SIBs, the obtained amorphous C displays an outstanding electrochem. performance including a high reversible capacity of 391 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 25 mA g-1 with a high ICE of 80%, and a superior cycling performance with a capacity retention of 97% after 100 cycles.  The high ICE is mainly attributed to the denser surface C layer which suppresses the penetration of electrolyte and fully uses the internal porosity.  The com. availability, and the desirable properties make this novel amorphous C-based anode a promising candidate for SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref40" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA08601A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Superior Low-cost Amorphous Carbon Anode Made from Pitch and Lignin for Sodium-ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A superior low-cost amorphous carbon anode made from pitch and lignin for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yunming; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Li, Hong; Chen, Liquan; Huang, Xuejie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are a promising candidate for grid electricity storage due to their potential low cost.  The development of anode materials is a crucial step to promote the commercialization of SIBs, and amorphous carbon materials are likely to be the most promising alternatives among all proposed anode materials.  However, the cost of the reported carbon materials is still very high due to the expensive precursors and their low carbon yield.  Here, we report an amorphous carbon (AC) material made from low cost pitch.  The amorphous carbon material with an amazing high carbon yield of 57% was achieved by utilizing the emulsification interaction between pitch and lignin to suppress the graphitization of pitch during the carbonization.  The effects of heat-treatment temps. and the pitch/lignin mass ratios on the morphol., microstructure and the electrochem. performance of AC were systematically investigated.  By optimizing exptl. conditions, we achieved one representative AC with a suitable morphol. and microstructure, which exhibits promising performances with a high reversible capacity of 254 mA h g-1, a high initial coulombic efficiency of 82% and excellent cycling stability.  This is the first demonstration that the pitch can be successfully applied in fabricating amorphous carbon anode materials for SIBs with superior low cost and high performance.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref41" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.08.119"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, B.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, Z.-Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chong, C.-B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Lignin-based Electrospun Carbon Nanofibrous Webs as Free-standing and Binder-free Electrodes for Sodium ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Low-cost and bio-based carbon nanofibrous webs (PL-CNFs) are fabricated from polyacrylonitrile (PAN)-refined lignin (RL) which is extd. from hardwood lignosulfonate via simple eletrospinning followed by stabilization and carbonization. (HTTs) in the range from 800, 1000 to 1300 °C on morphol. and structure of PL-CNFs are systematically studied.  Due to unique morphol. and weakly ordered turbostratic microstructure of the 3-D conductive composite networks, the PL-CNFs anode obtained at 1300 °C with a mass ratio of 5/5 exhibits a high reversible capacity of 292.6 mA h g-1 with an initial efficiency of 70.5% at a const. c.d. of 0.02 A g-1 when used as free-standing and binder-free anodes for sodium ion batteries (SIBs).         </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon with large interlayer spacing is suitable as the anode material for sodium-ion batteries. We prepd. hard carbon under different high-temp. treatment and biomass pretreatment conditions.  The graphitization degree of the hard carbon increased as the carbonization temp. increased; simultaneously, the reversible capacity for sodium storage was significantly influenced by the carbonization temp.  Structural characterization revealed differences in the structures of the hard carbons synthesized at different carbonization temps., which elucidates the correlation between the increased capacity and the micropore size available for sodium storage. These domains exhibit larger vol. with expanded the av. width (La), thickness (Lc) and the av. no. of graphite layers (n) when increasing the pyrolyzing temp.  When tested as anodes in Na-ion battery, the electrochem. results show the biomass C displays a superior specific capacity of 361 mAh/g at 50 mA/g. Herein, analogous graphite carbon sheets (AGCS) from corn stalks have been synthesized via a simple high temp. carbonization and expansion process.  A morphol. study showed that the obtained carbon sheets retained the natural cross-sectional honeycomb-like shape and the longitudinal hollow tubular array structure of the corn stalks, which provided abundant macropores and micropores to facilitate sodium ion transportation and electrolyte diffusion. What's more, a better rate capability for AGCS-1200 (232, 136 mA h g-1) than that of BMC-900 (125, 68 mA h g-1) at rates of 1C and 5C, resp., is demonstrated.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The utilization of renewable energies has become increasingly urgent for the sustainable development of our society.  Energy storage systems are essential in order to efficiently use these energies.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) show bright prospect in the application for energy storage markets due to the potential low cost originating from unlimited sources and wide distribution of Na.  However, the anode remains a great challenge in the industrialization of SIBs.  Hard carbon holds the most promising future among all reported anodes; however, there are still two main shortcomings such as high cost and low initial coulombic efficiency, which limit its application.  Here, we report a hard carbon material derived from an abundant and abandoned biomass of corn cobs (HCC) using a simple carbonization method.  The HCC shows excellent sodium storage performance with a reversible capacity of ca. 300 mA h g-1, a high initial coulombic efficiency of 86% and good cycling stability.  A prototype sodium-ion battery was prepd. to prove the application prospect using HCC1300 as the anode and Na0.9[Cu0.22Fe0.30Mn0.48]O2 as the cathode, exhibiting a high energy d. of 207 W h kg-1 and a long cycle life.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrochem. performance of nanospheric glucose derived hard carbon based electrodes, specially derived from D-glucose via hydrothermal carbonization and subsequent pyrolysis at 1100°C, has been studied in 1 M NaClO4 propylene carbonate electrolyte.                         cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A porous biomass-derived anode for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Youyu; Chen, Mingming; Li, Qi; Yuan, Chao; Wang, Chengyang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Although hard carbons have been turned out to be suitable for sodium storage, their high cost and low initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) need to be addressed for the com. application.  Here, we report an effective route including a pyrolysis process and a reductive strategy to synthesize high-performance hard carbons from waste apricot shell.  The obtained hard carbons inherit the unique architecture of the apricot shell, delivering a large interlayer spacing and a well-connected structure, which are beneficial for the Na+ intercalation and transport.  The anode performance is further enhanced by H2 redn. treatment, which efficiently reduces the defects and thus improves the ICE.  The final prepd. hard carbons exhibit a promising anode performance with a desirable reversible capacity of ca. 400 mAhg-1, an improved ICE of 79% and an excellent cycling stability.  This study should contribute to the better utilization of the biomass waste for the future large-scale application of sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref56" class="refNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit56" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201706294"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qi, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">N-Doping and Defective Nanographitic Domain Coupled Hard Carbon Nanoshells for High Performance Lithium/Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Adv.                 10.1016/j.jpowsour.2017.12.054</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D378%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D331-337%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DN.%2BZhang%26author%3DQ.%2BLiu%26author%3DW.%2BChen%26author%3DM.%2BWan%26author%3DX.%2BLi%26author%3DL.%2BWang%26author%3DL.%2BXue%26author%3DW.%2BZhang%26title%3DHigh%2BCapacity%2BHard%2BCarbon%2BDerived%2Bfrom%2BLotus%2BStem%2Bas%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2017.12.054&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c19199&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2017.12.054&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit57R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">57</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High capacity hard carbon derived from lotus stem as anode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Nan; Liu, Qing; Chen, Weilun; Wan, Min; Li, Xiaocheng; Wang, Lili; Xue, Lihong; Zhang, Wuxing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">378</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">331-337</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Porous hard carbons are synthesized via carbonizing lotus stems with naturally hierarchical structures.  The hard carbon carbonized at 1400°C (LS1400) delivers a total capacity 350 mAh/g in the c.d. of 100 mA/g and a plateau capacity of 250 mAh/g.  Even cycled at 100 mA/g after 450 cycles, the capacity still retains 94%.  Further investigation shows that the sodium storage of LS carbons involves Na+ adsorption in the defect sites, Na+ insertion and Na metal deposition in the closed pores.  However, the Na metal deposition in closed pores mainly contribute to the plateau capacity, leading to the excellent sodium storage performance of LS1400 with a large closed pore ratio of 66%.  The results show that the intrinsic structure of natural biomass can inspire us to design hard carbon with large closed pore ratio as excellent anode for sodium ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref58"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref58" class="refNumLink">58</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit58" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2017.11.054"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bao, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Rice Husk-derived Hard Carbons as High-performance Anode Materials for Sodium-ion Batteries</span>. <i>Carbon</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>127</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">658</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">666</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.carbon.2017.11.054</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D127%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D658-666%26journal%3DCarbon%26author%3DQ.%2BWang%26author%3DX.%2BZhu%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BFang%26author%3DX.%2BZhou%26author%3DJ.%2BBao%26title%3DRice%2BHusk-derived%2BHard%2BCarbons%2Bas%2BHigh-performance%2BAnode%2BMaterials%2Bfor%2BSodium-ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.carbon.2017.11.054&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c19199&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.carbon.2017.11.054&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit58R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">58</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rice husk-derived hard carbons as high-performance anode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Qiaoqiao; Zhu, Xiaoshu; Liu, Yuhan; Fang, Yuyan; Zhou, Xiaosi; Bao, Jianchun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">127</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">658-666</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CRBNAH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0008-6223</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have drawn ever-increasing attention for scalable elec. energy storage owing to the inexhaustible sources and wide distribution of sodium.  However, to develop feasible anode materials still remains a great challenge for the practical application of SIBs.  Here, the authors report hard carbons derived from a plentiful and deserted biomass of rice husk through a facile acid treatment and subsequent pyrolysis.  The study illustrates that the electrochem. properties of the rice husk-derived hard carbons (RHHCs) are significantly influenced by the pyrolysis temp. because of the discrepancy in their microstructure.  The RHHC pyrolyzed at 1300° (RHHC-1300) shows the highest reversible capacity of 372 mAh/g and good cycling stability and rate performance due to its large interlayer distance and suitable oxygen content.  Also, full sodium-ion batteries are assembled to examine the application prospect using Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C and RHHC-1300 as cathode and anode materials, resp., delivering a high-energy d. of 185 Wh/kg and stable cycling performance.  This work could intensify the fundamental understanding of the sodium storage mechanism in biomass-derived hard carbons.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref59"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref59" class="refNumLink">59</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit59" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.7b14776"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yoon, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hwang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Carbon with Expanded and Well-Developed Graphene Planes Derived Directly from Condensed Lignin as a High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit59R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">59</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon with Expanded and Well-Developed Graphene Planes Derived Directly from Condensed Lignin as a High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yoon, Dohyeon; Hwang, Jieun; Chang, Wonyoung; Kim, Jaehoon</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">569-581</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this study, we demonstrate that lignin, which constitutes 30-40 wt % of the terrestrial lignocellulosic biomass and is produced from second generation biofuel plants as a cheap byproduct, is an excellent precursor material for sodium-ion battery (NIB) anodes.  Because it is rich in arom. monomers that are highly cross-linked by ether and condensed bonds, the lignin material carbonized at 1300 °C (C-1300) in this study has small graphitic domains with well-developed graphene layers, a large interlayer spacing (0.403 nm), and a high micropore surface area (207.5 m2 g-1).  When tested as an anode in an NIB, C-1300 exhibited an initial Coulombic efficiency of 68% and a high reversible capacity of 297 mA h g-1 at 50 mA g-1 after 50 cycles.  The high capacity of 199 mA h g-1 at less than 0.1 V with a flat voltage profile and an extremely low charge-discharge voltage hysteresis (&lt;0.03 V) make C-1300 a promising energy-dense electrode material.  In addn., C-1300 exhibited an excellent high-rate performance of 116 mA h g-1 at 2.5 A g-1 and showed stable cycling retention (0.2% capacity decay per cycle after 500 cycles).  By comparing the properties of the lignin-derived carbon with oak sawdust-derived and sugar-derived carbons and a low-temp. carbonized sample (900 °C), the reasons for the excellent performance of C-1300 were detd. to result from facilitated Na+-ion transport to the graphitic layer and the microporous regions that penetrate through the less defective and enlarged interlayer spacings.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref60"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref60" class="refNumLink">60</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit60" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2017.08.030"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-yield Humic Acid-based Hard Carbons as Promising Anode Materials for Sodium-ion Batteries</span>. <i>Carbon</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>123</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">727</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">734</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A low-cost and sustainable anode material is essential for the future commercialization of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Among all proposed anode materials for SIBs, hard carbons are considered to hold the most promise.  However, high cost and low carbon yield of precursors limit its industrialization process.  Here the synthesis of a biomass-derived hard carbon from leonardite humic acid (LHA) through a facile process was reported.                         cas_cit62R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">62</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Expanded biomass-derived hard carbon with ultra-stable performance in sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Ziyi; Liang, Feng; Zhou, Zhongren; Zeng, Xiaoyuan; Wang, Ding; Dong, Peng; Zhao, Jinbao; Sun, Shigang; Zhang, Yingjie; Li, Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

                        cas_cit64R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">64</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A high-performance sodium-ion battery enhanced by macadamia shell derived hard carbon anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zheng, Yuheng; Wang, Yuesheng; Lu, Yaxiang; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Li, Ju</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">39</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">489-498</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIB) have usually been tested in half-cells by cycling between 0-2 V, and is believed to exhibit low rate capability.  However, we find that the specific capacity, the rate performance, and the cycling performance may all be severely underestimated with the traditional half-cell cycling evaluation method, due to premature truncation of part II of the capacity (part I is "sloping", part II is "plateauing", while part III is Na metal deposition).  Here we introduce a sodium-matched SIB full-cell architecture, with newly developed hard carbon derived from macadamia shell (MHC) as anode and Na[Cu1/9Ni2/9Fe1/3Mn1/3]O2 (NCNFM) as the cathode material, with anode/cathode areal capacity ratio of 1.02-1.04.  Our carefully balanced full-cells exhibit a cell-level theor. specific energy of 215 Wh kg-1 at C/10 and 186 Wh kg-1 at 1C based on cathode-active and anode-active material wts., and an outstanding capacity retention of 70% after 1300 cycles ( ∼ 2000h).  Traditional half-cell test (THT) of MHC using superabundant Na metal counter electrode shows only 51.7 mAh g-1 capacity at 1C, and appears to die in no more than 100 h due to low open-circuit voltage slope and large polarization.  A revised half-cell test (RHT) which shows much better agreements with full-cell test results, delivers a specific capacity of 314 mAh g-1, with an initial Coulombic efficiency of ∼ 91.4%, which is comparable to that of graphite anode in lithium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref65"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref65" class="refNumLink">65</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit65" data-doi="10.1016/0022-4596(77)90006-8"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Weppner, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huggins, R. Solid State Chem.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">1977</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>22</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">297</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">308</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/0022-4596(77)90006-8</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D22%26publication_year%3D1977%26pages%3D297-308%26journal%3DJ.%2BSolid%2BState%2BChem.%26author%3DW.%2BWeppner%26author%3DR.%2BA.%2BHuggins%26title%3DElectrochemical%2BInvestigation%2Bof%2Bthe%2BChemical%2BDiffusion%252C%2BPartial%2BIonic%2BConductivities%252C%2Band%2BOther%2BKinetic%2BParameters%2Bin%2BLi3Sb%2Band%2BLi3Bi%26doi%3D10.1016%252F0022-4596%252877%252990006-8&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c19199&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2F0022-4596%2877%2990006-8&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit65R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">65</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical investigation of the chemical diffusion, partial ionic conductivities, and other kinetic parameters in lithium antimonide (Li3Sb) and lithium bismuthide (Li3Bi)</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Weppner, W.; Huggins, R. A.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Solid State Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1977</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">22</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">297-308</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JSSCBI</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0022-4596</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">A galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique (GITT) was used to electrochem. det. the chem. and component diffusion coeffs., the elec. and general Li mobilities, the partial Li ionic cond., the parabolic tarnishing rate const., and the thermodn. enhancement factor in Li3Sb and Li3Bi as a function of stoichiometry in the temp. range from 360 to 600°.  LiCl, KCl eutectic melts were used as electrolytes and Al, LiAl 2-phase mixts. as solid ref. and counter electrodes.  The stoichiometric range of the Sb compd. is rather small, 7 × 10-3 at 360°, whereas the Bi compd. has a range of 0.22 (380°), mostly on the Li deficit side of the ideal compn.  The thermodn. enhancement factor in Li3Sb depends strongly on the stoichiometry, and has a peak value of nearly 70,000; for Li3Bi it rises more smoothly to a max. of 360.  The chem. diffusion coeff. for Li3Sb is 2 × 10-5 cm2 s-1 at neg. deviations from the ideal stoichiometry and increases by about an order of magnitude in the presence of excess Li at 360°.  The corresponding value for Li3Bi is 10-4 cm2 s-1 with high Li deficit, and increases markedly when approaching ideal stoichiometry.  The activation energies are small, 0.1-0.3 eV, depending on the stoichiometry, in both phases.  The mobility of Li in Li3Bi is ∼500 fold greater than in Li3Sb with a Li deficit.  The parabolic tarnishing rate const. shows a sharp increase at higher Li activities in Li3Sb whereas in Li3Bi it has a roughly linear dependence upon the logarithm of the Li activity.  Because of the fast ionic transport in these mixed conducting materials, Li3Sb and Li3Bi may be called fast electrodes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref66"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref66" class="refNumLink">66</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit66" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201900550"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Adams, R. A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Varma, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pol, V. G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Carbon Anodes for Nonaqueous Alkali Metal-Ion Batteries and Their Thermal Safety Aspects</span>. <i>Adv. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>9</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1900550</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/aenm.201900550</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D9%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D1900550%26journal%3DAdv.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26author%3DR.%2BA.%2BAdams%26author%3DA.%2BVarma%26author%3DV.%2BG.%2BPol%26title%3DCarbon%2BAnodes%2Bfor%2BNonaqueous%2BAlkali%2BMetal-Ion%2BBatteries%2Band%2BTheir%2BThermal%2BSafety%2BAspects%26doi%3D10.1002%252Faenm.201900550&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c19199&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Faenm.201900550&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The increasing interest in energy storage for the grid can be attributed to multiple factors, including the capital costs of managing peak demands, the investments needed for grid reliability, and the integration of renewable energy sources.  Although existing energy storage is dominated by pumped hydroelec., there is the recognition that battery systems can offer a no. of high-value opportunities, provided that lower costs can be obtained.  The battery systems reviewed here include sodium-sulfur batteries that are com. available for grid applications, redox-flow batteries that offer low cost, and lithium-ion batteries whose development for com. electronics and elec. vehicles is being applied to grid storage.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202101972"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultralong Cycle Life Organic Cathode Enabled by Ether-Based Electrolytes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultralong Cycle Life Organic Cathode Enabled by Ether-Based Electrolytes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Yuqing; Bai, Panxing; Li, Benfang; Zhao, Chen; Chen, Zifeng; Li, Mengjie; Su, Hai; Yang, Jixing; Xu, Yunhua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Org. cathode materials have gained substantial attention in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) because of their low cost, structure versatility, and environmental friendliness.  Nevertheless, the use of org. materials is plagued by the unsatisfactory cycling performance caused by dissoln. of org. electrode materials, use of inappropriate electrolytes, and/or poor interfacial compatibility.  In this work, an ultralong cycle life of SIBs through coupling an insol. org. cathode, N, N'-bis(glycinyl) naphthalene diimide, with ether-based electrolytes, is realized.  A thin and stable inorg.-rich solid electrolyte interphase is constructed through a prior redn. of salt in the org. solvents in the ether-based electrolytes, promising fast charge transfer kinetics and stable cycling performance of org. electrodes in SIBs.  A superb long cycle life of 70 000 cycles at 10C is demonstrated, which is a new record for org. cathode materials in SIBs.  The findings highlight the key role of electrolytes and electrolyte/electrode interfaces in furthering the practical prospects of org. electrodes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1126/science.270.5236.590"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dahn, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review with 24 refs. of mechanisms for lithium insertion in carbonaceous materials.  Lithium can be inserted reversibly within most carbonaceous materials.  The phys. mechanism for this insertion depends on the carbon type.  Lithium intercalates in layered carbons, e.g., graphite, and it adsorbs on the surfaces of single carbon layers in nongraphitizable hard carbons.  Lithium also appears to reversibly bind near hydrogen atoms in carbonaceous materials contg. substantial hydrogen, which are made by heating org. precursors to temps. near 700°.  Each of these three classes of materials is suitable for use as anode in advanced lithium batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1038/s41467-018-06126-z"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guan, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ming, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mai, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Lithiophilic-lithiophobic Gradient Interfacial Layer for a Highly Stable Lithium Metal Anode</span>. <i>Nat.                         rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Lithiophilic-lithiophobic gradient interfacial layer for a highly stable lithium metal anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang Huimin; Xiang Yu; Li Meng; Zhang Wenfeng; Zhu Xiayu; Ming Hai; Lu Lin; Qiu Jingyi; Cao Gaoping; Yang Yusheng; Zhang Hao; Zhang Huimin; Liao Xiaobin; Mai Liqiang; Liao Xiaobin; Zhao Yan; Guan Yuepeng; Huang Yaqin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3729</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">The long-standing issue of lithium dendrite growth during repeated deposition or dissolution processes hinders the practical use of lithium-metal anodes for high-energy density batteries.  Here, we demonstrate a promising lithiophilic-lithiophobic gradient interfacial layer strategy in which the bottom lithiophilic zinc oxide/carbon nanotube sublayer tightly anchors the whole layer onto the lithium foil, facilitating the formation of a stable solid electrolyte interphase, and prevents the formation of an intermediate mossy lithium corrosion layer.  Together with the top lithiophobic carbon nanotube sublayer, this gradient interfacial layer can effectively suppress dendrite growth and ensure ultralong-term stable lithium stripping/plating.  This strategy is further demonstrated to provide substantially improved cycle performance in copper current collector, 10 cm(2) pouch cell and lithium-sulfur batteries, which, coupled with a simple fabrication process and wide applicability in various materials for lithium-metal protection, makes the lithiophilic-lithiophobic gradient interfacial layer a favored strategy for next-generation lithium-metal batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201703268"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Saurel, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Orayech, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Carriazo, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rojo, T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">From Charge Storage Mechanism to Performance: A Roadmap toward High Specific Energy Sodium-Ion Batteries through Carbon Anode Optimization</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Phosphorus-based anodes for alkali metal-ion batteries are attractive due to their high theor.-specific capacity.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbons attract myriad interest as anode materials for high-energy rechargeable batteries due to their low costs and high theor. capacities; practically, they deliver unsatisfactory performance due to their intrinsically disordered microarchitecture.  Here a facile ion-catalyzed synthesis is reported of a phenol-formaldehyde resin-based hard-carbon aerogel that takes advantage of the chelation effect of phenol and Fe3+, which consists of a three-dimensionally interconnected carbon network embedded with hydrogen-rich, ordered microstructures of expanded nanographites and carbon micropores. The structural merits of the carbon offer chances to achieve lithium/sodium storage performance far beyond that possible with the conventional carbon anode materials, including graphite and mesocarbon microbeads, along with fast kinetics and long cycle life.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are expected to be a promising com. alternative to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) for large-scale and low-cost elec. energy storage applications in the near future.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are expected to be a promising com. alternative to lithium-ion batteries for grid electricity storage due to their potential low cost in the near future.  Up to the present, the anode material still remains a great challenge for the application of SIBs, esp. at room temp.  Graphite has an obvious limitation to store larger radius sodium ions (Na+) in comparison with lithium ions (Li+), while the hard carbon with large interlayer distance can demonstrate a relatively high storage capability and durable cycle life.  However, the disadvantages of low initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) mainly caused by large surface area and high cost synthetic approach hinder its practical applications.  Herein, a new coupled carbonization strategy is presented to prep. a cost-effective hard carbon material by pyrolyzing and carbonizing the mixt. of abundant sucrose and phenolic resin.  Benefiting from the specialized pyrolysis reaction process and optimized conditions as studied in detail, the hard carbon has an extremely low surface area of 1.54 m2 g-1 and high initial Coulombic efficiency of 87%, which have been rarely reported before and enhance the utilization efficiency of Na+ consumption within the cathode in the future.  More importantly, the hard carbon, with a high interlayer distance 3.95 Å, can deliver a higher capacity of 319 mAh/g and maintain a finer capacity retention of 90% over 150 cycles.  Besides, a full cell with the configuration of as-prepd. hard carbon anode vs. an air-stable O3-Na0.9[Cu0.22Fe0.30Mn0.48]O2 cathode is further presented, and it has a high ICE of 80% and energy d. of 256 Wh kganode-1 (vs hard carbon) with reliable cycle performance.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Monodispersed hollow polymer microspheres (HPMs) and hollow carbon microspheres (HCMs) are prepd. by a low-cost and rapid spray-drying technique using resorcinol-formaldehyde as precursors.  By spraying the precursor soln. into a high-temp. chamber, micrometer-scale hollow structure can be immediately obtained.  To achieve the required morphol., the factors of influencing the products morphol. and purity are systematically optimized.  The as-obtained HPMs have a low bulk d. of 0.089 g/cm3, narrow particle size distribution of 15-80 μm with a mean size of 37 μm, a high floatation ratio of 96.3% and high mech. strength.  Followed by a simple carbonization, HCMs with a bulk d. of ca. 0.1 g/cm3 and a mean size of 23 μm are achieved.  This spray-drying strategy could drastically reduce their prodn. times and costs, enabling continuous and scalable synthesis of hollow microspheres for practical use.  As a proof-of-concept application, a series of syntactic foam consisting of HPMs and HCMs as fillers and phenolic resin as matrix are prepd. via a hot-press molding.  The resulting composite materials have low bulk densities but improved mech. properties, which highlights the possibility for the manufg. of light-wt. materials using these kinds of hollow microspheres.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref31" class="rightTabRefNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit31" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201502449"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Prototype Sodium-Ion Batteries Using an Air-Stable and Co/Ni-Free O3-Layered Metal Oxide Cathode</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A series of hard carbon nanofiber-based electrodes derived from electrospun polyacrylonitrile nanofibers have been fabricated by stabilization in air at about 280° and then carbonization in N2 at heat treatment temps. between 800 and 1500°.  The electrochem. performances of the binder-free, current collector-free carbon nanofiber-based anodes in lithium-ion batteries and sodium-ion batteries are systematically investigated and compared.  We demonstrate the presence of similar alkali metal insertion mechanisms in both cases, but just the differences of the layer spacing and pore size available for lithium and sodium ion lead the discharge capacity delivered at sloping region and plateau region to vary from the kinds of alkali elements.  Although the anodes in sodium-ion batteries show poorer rate capability than that in lithium-ion batteries, they still achieve a reversible sodium intercalation capacity of 275 mA-h/g and similar cycling stability due to the conductive three-dimensional network, weakly ordered turbostratic structure and a large interlayer spacing between graphene sheets.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon nanoparticles (HCNP) were synthesized by the pyrolysis of a polyaniline precursor.  The measured Na+ cation diffusion coeff.
